Historically described as a highly alcoholic spirit, it is 45–74% ABV (alcohol by volume). Absinthe traditionally has a natural green color but may also be colorless. It is commonly referred to in historical literature as la fée verte 'the green fairy'. While sometimes casually referred to as a liqueur, absinthe unlike pastis is not usually bottled with sugar or sweeteners. Historically described as a highly alcoholic spirit, it is 45–74% ABV (alcohol by volume). Absinthe traditionally has a natural green color but may also be colorless. It is commonly referred to in historical literature as la fée verte 'the green fairy'. While sometimes casually referred to as a liqueur, absinthe unlike pastis is not usually bottled with sugar or sweeteners. Absinthe is traditionally bottled at a high level of alcohol by volume, but it is normally diluted with water before being consumed.","refs":[],"parents":[],"slug":"absinthe","type":"category"}],"slug":"vieux-pontarlier-absinthe","refs":[],"ingredients":[],"quantity":{"amount":1,"unit":"tsp"}},{"$schema":"../../../schemas/ingredient.schema.json","name":"Barbancourt White","type":"spirit","categories":[{"$schema":"../../schemas/category.schema.json","name":"Rhum Agricole Blanc","categoryType":"spirit","description":"Rhum agricole is the French term for sugarcane juice rum, a style of rum originally distilled in the French Caribbean islands from freshly squeezed sugarcane juice rather than molasses.
